> We have at this present what to answer to men of a contrary faction, always objecting,[note 35.3] either our Elders are damned altogether, it were wicked to condemn all, they be saved therefore. But they have not heard of that our new doctrine, but kept the old, in the old therefore shall we also be saved. To this we make answer, that our elders were saved, we grant gladly, and believe it also: but we add, of the free grace of God, as we shall by and by more plainly vnderſtade: and not by popiſh superstition: neither therefore shalt thou by the same be saved: but thou must also be saved by Christ, if thou wilt be saved. But rather saying at this day through the singular goodness of God, the gospel is preached, and is preached even to thee, to the which thou show thy self a rebel, thou declare thy self to be none of the nubre of gods children,[note 35.4] which hear the word of God with joy, and keep it. Neither shalt thou have any cloak or pretenſe wherewith to excuse thy sin. If thy forefathers had had the like opportunity, which thou neglect, good God, what a space wold they have run before thee? Therefore thou both willing and witting, speak against God, and wilfully throw thy self into destruction. Dye therefore through thine own fault.

**Modern English:**

We have at this present what to answer to people of a contrary faction, always objecting that either our Elders are damned altogether; it were wicked to condemn all, they be saved therefore. But they have not heard of that our new doctrine, but kept the old, in the old therefore shall we also be saved. To this we make answer, that our elders were saved, we grant gladly, and believe it also: but we add, by the free grace of God, as we shall by and by more plainly understand; and not by popish superstition. Neither therefore shalt thou by the same be saved: but thou must also be saved by Christ, if thou wilt be saved. But rather saying at this day through the singular goodness of God, the gospel is preached, and is preached even to thee, to which thou showest thyself a rebel, thou declarest thyself to be none of the number of God’s children, which hear the word of God with joy, and keep it. Neither shalt thou have any cloak or pretense wherewith to excuse thy sin. If thy forefathers had had the like opportunity, which thou neglect, good God, what a space would they have run before thee? Therefore thou both willingly and knowingly speak against God, and wilfully throw thyself into destruction. Die therefore through thine own fault.

---

### Paragraph 490

**Original (1561):**

> [note 35.5]Neither doth this place only testify, very many to be saved by the grace of God from corruption, and in the true faith, even than, what time in mans judgment there appear none or very few to be faithful: and even very few or none to be saved, by reason of the exceading great corruption of every time? We have also heard and red in the.3. book of kings the.19. Chapter. that Helias complaining most grievously of the ſcarſetie of the faithful, understood, that God had reserved yet ſeue thousand men, which had not boughed their knees before Baal. The lord therefore hath evermore his chosen, which in the midst of destruction and perdition by grace through Christ are saved.

**Modern English:**

Nor does this passage testify only that many will be saved by God’s grace from corruption and in the true faith, even when, in human judgment, no one or very few appear faithful; and even when very few or none seem to be saved because of the exceedingly great corruption of every age? We have also heard and read in the third book of Kings, chapter 19, that Elijah, complaining bitterly about the scarcity of the faithful, understood that God had reserved seven thousand men who had not bowed their knees before Baal. Therefore, the Lord always has his elect, who, through grace in Christ, are saved in the midst of destruction and ruin.

---

### Paragraph 491

**Original (1561):**

> [note 35.6]And the Author of this salvation and preſeruatio is first declared to be an Angel aſcendyng from the rising of the sun: to wit the Lord Christ that sun of rightuouſenes, rising up in those most thick Antichristian darkness, to those that seek God, and lighting them the darkness drive away. For Christ is the true light of all times, lighting all, so many as be illumined. He gives his people also preachers, which by the word may defend Gods people, that they be not destroyed with that common destruction.

**Modern English:**

[note 35.6]And the Author of this salvation and preservation is first declared to be an angel ascending from the rising of the sun: namely, the Lord Christ, that sun of righteousness, rising up in those most intense Antichristian darkness, to those who seek God, and driving away the darkness for them. For Christ is the true light of all times, illuminating all who are illuminated. He gives his people also preachers, who by the word may defend God’s people, that they be not destroyed with that common destruction.

---
